style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.98em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -5.168em; left: 3.412em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-78"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-79" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: STIXGeneral-Regular;">2</span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 3.98em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.219em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -1.122em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 3.066em;"></span></span></nobr><span class="MJX_Assistive_MathML MJX_Assistive_MathML_Block" role="presentation"><math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>D</mi></mrow><mrow><msup><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mfrac><mrow><mn>4</mn></mrow><mrow><mi>π</mi><mi>τ</mi></mrow></mfrac><msup><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="true">(</mo><mfrac><mrow><msub><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi></mrow></msub><msub><mrow><mi>V</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></msub></mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mi>M</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi></mrow></msub><mi>S</mi></mrow></mfrac><mo stretchy="true">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="true">(</mo><mfrac><mrow><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi></mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mi>E</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi></mrow></msub></mrow></msub></mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi></mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mi>E</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi></mrow></msub></mrow></msub></mrow></mfrac><mo stretchy="true">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></math></span></span></div><script type="math/mml" id="MathJax-Element-1"><math display="block" indentalign="left"><mrow><mrow><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><msub><mrow><mi>D</mi></mrow><mrow><msup><mrow><mi>Na</mi></mrow><mrow><mo>+</mo></mrow></msup></mrow></msub></mstyle></mrow></mrow><mrow><mo linebreak="nobreak">=</mo><mstyle indentshift="3em" indentshiftlast="3em"><mfrac><mrow><mn>4</mn></mrow><mrow><mi>π</mi><mi>τ</mi></mrow></mfrac><msup><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="true">(</mo><mfrac><mrow><msub><mrow><mi>m</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi></mrow></msub><msub><mrow><mi>V</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">m</mi></mrow></msub></mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mi>M</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">B</mi></mrow></msub><mi>S</mi></mrow></mfrac><mo stretchy="true">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup><msup><mrow><mrow><mo stretchy="true">(</mo><mfrac><mrow><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi></mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mi>E</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">s</mi></mrow></msub></mrow></msub></mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">Δ</mi></mrow><mrow><msub><mrow><mi>E</mi></mrow><mrow><mi mathvariant="normal">t</mi></mrow></msub></mrow></msub></mrow></mfrac><mo stretchy="true">)</mo></mrow></mrow><mrow><mn>2</mn></mrow></msup></mstyle></mrow></math></script></div><div class="label"><span class="labelSpan">(1)</span></div></div>In this analysis, we define several key parameters to quantify the transport properties of sodium ions in hard carbon materials. Among them, the relaxation time τ, the active material mass <i>m</i><sub>B</sub>, the molar mass of the active material <i>M</i><sub>B</sub>, the molar volume of the hard carbon <i>V</i><sub>m</sub>, and the surface area of the active material <i>S</i> play an important role. In addition, the Δ<sub><i>E</i><sub>s</sub></sub> and Δ<sub><i>E</i><sub>t</sub></sub> parameters obtained from the constant current intermittent titration (GITT <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/suppl_file/la4c03504_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/suppl_file/la4c03504_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>) curve are of critical importance.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/asset/images/medium/la4c03504_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/asset/images/large/la4c03504_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a) Impedance plots of the ZJ-1500-HCl electrode, presented before, at the 10th, 50th and 100th cycles. (b)  Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient of the ZJ-1500-HCl. (c) CV curves of the ZJ-1500-HCl electrode for the first three cycles, presented at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (d) CV curves of the ZJ-1500-HCl for different scanning rates, presented from 0.1 to 2.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (e) The relationship between log(<i>v</i>) and log(<i>I</i>) of ZJ-1500-HCl, calculated from the CV curves at different scan rates from 0.1 to 2.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. (f) The ratio of the contribution of the capacitance and diffusion control charge of ZJ-1500-HCl at different scan rates.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/asset/images/large/la4c03504_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Based on these parameters, the calculated distribution of the diffusion coefficient <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> for sodium ions falls within the range of 10<sup>–11</sup> to 10<sup>–9</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>b. Compared with ZJ-1500-HCl, the continuity of diffusion coefficient of ZJ-1500 is poorer (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/suppl_file/la4c03504_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S7 and S13</a>, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/suppl_file/la4c03504_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). This diffusive behavior of sodium ions indicates that the electrode material has excellent electrochemical reaction kinetics, which is attributed to the fast migration of sodium ions within the active material.</div><div class="NLM_p">Due to the efficient diffusion of sodium ions in the hard carbon material, the electrode material exhibits excellent multiplicative performance. it maintains a stable electrochemical response at high current densities. This means that the electrode material can maintain good energy storage capacity and cycling stability even under rapid charge and discharge conditions, which is extremely beneficial in practical applications, especially for sodium-ion battery systems that require high performance.</div><div class="NLM_p"><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>c illustrates the CV curves of ZJ-1500-HCl for the initial three revolutions at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. The oxidation of sodium ions occurs at 0.1 V, while their reduction takes place at 0.01 V, resulting in the formation of a pair of typical oxidation–reduction peaks. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref50" aria-label="reference 50">(50)</a> Furthermore, the scan curves of the subsequent cycles exhibited a high degree of overlap, indicating that the ZJ-1500-HCl electrode demonstrated excellent reversibility during the processes of charging and discharging. The CV curves of ZJ-1500-HCl at varying scan rates, spanning from 0.1 to 2.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, are illustrated in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>d. As the scan rate increases, the peak height gradually rises. Compared with ZJ-1500-HCl, ZJ-1500 is less stable (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/suppl_file/la4c03504_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S9 and S10</a>, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/suppl_file/la4c03504_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). However, at higher scan rates, the peak shifts more slowly, indicating a smooth polarization.</div><div class="NLM_p">Whether the capacity of a cell is surface-controlled or diffusion-controlled can be determined by the equation <i>I</i> = <i>av</i><sup><i>b</i></sup>, where <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> are constants; <i>I</i> and <i>v</i> are the peak current and scan rate, respectively. Typically, a value of the fitting exponent <i>b</i> close to 1.0 indicates that the material is subjected to surface processes contributing to the capacity, while a value close to 0.5 indicates that the material is subjected to diffusion-controlled processes contributing to the capacity. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref51 ref52" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref51 ref52" aria-label="reference 51 and 52">(51,52)</a> The <i>b</i> values of ZJ-1500-HCl at peaks 1 and 2 were fitted by several cv curves with different scan rates of 0.54 and 0.5, respectively, as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>e. The slopes of the lines of the two ZJ-1500 peaks differ greatly, and the redox overlap is not high (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/suppl_file/la4c03504_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S11</a>, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/suppl_file/la4c03504_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). It indicates that the main capacity contribution of ZJ-1500-HCl is diffusion-controlled, and the peaks of the redox peaks are all below 0.1 V, so the anode’s plateau capacity accounts for a greater proportion.</div><div class="NLM_p last">The distribution of the capacitive contributions at scan rates of 0.1–2 mV s<sup>–1</sup> was calculated as shown in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure 4</a>f, and the percentage of capacitive contributions gradually increased with the increase in scan rate. The pseudocapacitance of the ZJ-1500 varies more with increasing scan rate and is unstable (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/suppl_file/la4c03504_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S12</a>, <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504/suppl_file/la4c03504_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Supporting Information</a>). ZJ-1500-HCl has a good microstructure, which is mainly controlled by diffusion to contribute to the capacity, smaller resistivity, and suitable ion diffusion coefficients, which makes it superior to other materials in long cycle stability, first time Coulombic efficiency, and multiplicity performance.</div></div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i11">Conclusion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, the pore structure, degree of disorder, and interlayer spacing of the sour date shell-derived hard carbon material were successfully improved using a simple acid treatment method. This series of physical property optimizations collectively contributed to the material’s performance in electrochemical energy storage applications, in particular enhancing its potential as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries. The increase in porosity and interlayer spacing not only facilitates full infiltration of the electrolyte but also provides a smoother path for the embedding and de-embedding of sodium ions, while the increase in disorder level contributes to the improvement of the electrochemical activity and cycling stability of the material. This enhancement facilitates  improvement of the sodium storage capacity. The optimized sample exhibited an ICE of up to 94.1% at a current density of 20 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, an increase in reversible specific capacity of 30.4 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> and good long-period performance. The reversible specific capacity retention efficiency increased by 73.39% at a current density of 300 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, and the multiplicity performance was much better than that of the unpickled sample. The composition of the SEI was analyzed by HRTEM, which revealed that the SEI membrane was 25% thinner after acid washing. This finding suggests that a thinner SEI membrane may improve the first Coulomb efficiency, thereby facilitating fast sodium ion transport and maintaining the efficiency over extended cycling periods. While there are numerous types of biomass-derived hard carbon anode materials, it is my contention that those derived from sour date flesh will play a role in the future. It is my hope that further research will yield more effective and commercially viable materials in the future.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i12">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge at <a href="/doi/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504?goto=supporting-info" class="ext-link">https://pubs.acs.org/doi/10.1021/acs.langmuir.4c03504</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Material characterization;                         cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Inexpensive and eco-friendly nanostructured birnessite-type δ-MnO2: A design strategy from oxygen defect engineering and K+ pre-intercalation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lv, Wei; Meng, Jingwen; Li, Yiming; Yang, Weijie; Tian, Yonglan; Lyu, Xuefeng; Duan, Congwen; Ma, Xiaolei; Wu, Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">98</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">107274</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanostructured birnessite-type δ-MnO2 (KMO-V) with intercalated K+ and oxygen vacancies is synthesized by a hydrothermal method at 160 °C followed by annealing under 300 °C in Ar atm. with non-toxic and inexpensive γ-MnO2 (Unit price: 0.96-1.6 US$ Kg-1) as raw material.  The interplanar spacing in (001) diffraction direction of KMO-V is near 0.719 nm.  The considerable initial discharge potential of about 1.8 V, specific energy of 389.88 Wh kg-1, and cyclic stability of 91.9% after 1500 cycles at 1.0 A g-1 of KMO-V are obtained.  A hybrid intercalation mechanism of H+ and Zn2+ is revealed, KMO-V has the best diffusion kinetics performance of Zn2+ among the samples according to the calcn. based on d. functional theory (DFT).  The byproduct Zn4(OH)6SO4·4H2O and Mn2+ are thought to be the primary factors of capacity decay, the synergy of K+ pre-intercalation and oxygen vacancies plays a crit. role of enhancing structural stability and reaction kinetics in KMO-V.  Thus, this work provides an eco-friendly research method of inexpensive electrode material in aq. Zn-ion batteries (AZIBs) for large-scale energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref5" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2024.01.085"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Organic polymer coating induced multiple heteroatom-doped carbon framework confined Co1-xS@ NPSC core-shell hexapod for advanced sodium/potassium ion batteries</span>. <i>J. Rev.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2020</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>120</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">6358</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.chemrev.9b00463</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D120%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D6358%26journal%3DChem.%2BRev.%26author%3DT.%2BHosaka%26author%3DK.%2BKubota%26author%3DA.%2BS.%2BHameed%26author%3DS.%2BKomaba%26title%3DResearch%2Bdevelopment%2Bon%2BK-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.chemrev.9b00463&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.chemrev.9b00463&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Research Development on K-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hosaka, Tomooki; Kubota, Kei; Hameed, A. Shahul; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">120</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6358-6466</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CHREAY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0009-2665</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Li-ion batteries (LIBs), commercialized in 1991, have the highest energy d. among practical secondary batteries and are widely utilized in electronics, elec. vehicles, and even stationary energy storage systems.  Along with the expansion of their demand and application, concern about the resources of Li and Co is growing.  Therefore, secondary batteries composed of earth-abundant elements are desired to complement LIBs.  In recent years, K-ion batteries (KIBs) have attracted significant attention as potential alternatives to LIBs.  Previous studies have developed pos. and neg. electrode materials for KIBs and demonstrated several unique advantages of KIBs over LIBs and Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  Thus, besides being free from any scarce/toxic elements, the low std. electrode potentials of K/K+ electrodes lead to high operation voltages competitive to those obsd. in LIBs.  Moreover, K+ ions exhibit faster ionic diffusion in electrolytes due to weaker interaction with solvents and anions than that of Li+ ions; this is essential to realize high-power KIBs.  This review comprehensively covers the studies on electrochem. materials for KIBs, including electrode and electrolyte materials and a discussion on recent achievements and remaining/emerging issues.  The review also includes insights into electrode reactions and solid-state ionics and nonaq. soln. chem. as well as perspectives on the research-based development of KIBs compared to those of LIBs and NIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref16" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.3390/molecules28104027"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hard-carbon negative electrodes from biomasses for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Molecules</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>28</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4027</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.3390/molecules28104027</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D4027%26journal%3DMolecules%26author%3DB.%2BLu%26author%3DC.%2BLin%26author%3DH.%2BXiong%26author%3DC.%2BZhang%26author%3DL.%2BFang%26author%3DJ.%2BSun%26author%3DZ.%2BHu%26author%3DY.%2BWu%26author%3DX.%2BFan%26author%3DG.%2BLi%26title%3DHard-carbon%2Bnegative%2Belectrodes%2Bfrom%2Bbiomasses%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.3390%252Fmolecules28104027&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.3390%2Fmolecules28104027&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1021/acssuschemeng.2c04750"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Spiering, G.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Low-Cost and High-Performance Hard Carbon Anode Materials for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Kun; Jin, Yu; Sun, Shixiong; Huang, Yangyang; Peng, Jian; Luo, Jiahuan; Zhang, Qin; Qiu, Yuegang; Fang, Chun; Han, Jiantao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Omega</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1687-1695</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACSODF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2470-1343</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As an anode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), hard carbon (HC) presents high specific capacity and favorable cycling performance.  However, high cost and low initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of HC seriously limit its future commercialization for SIBs.  A typical biowaste, mangosteen shell was selected as a precursor to prep. low-cost and high-performance HC via a facile one-step carbonization method, and the influence of different heat treatments on the morphologies, microstructures, and electrochem. performances was investigated systematically.  The microstructure evolution studied using X-ray diffraction, Raman, Brunauer-Emmett-Teller, and high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, along with electrochem. measurements, reveals the optimal carbonization condition of the mangosteen shell: HC carbonized at 1500 °C for 2 h delivers the highest reversible capacity of ∼330 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, a capacity retention of ∼98% after 100 cycles, and an ICE of ∼83%.  Addnl., the sodium-ion storage behavior of HC is deeply analyzed using galvanostatic intermittent titrn. and cyclic voltammetry technologies.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref22" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.3390/molecules28083595"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, N. J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Modulating the graphitic domains and pore structure of corncob-derived hard carbons by pyrolysis to improve sodium storage</span>. <i>Molecules.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>28</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3595</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.3390/molecules28083595</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3D3595%26journal%3DMolecules.%26author%3DN.%2BJ.%2BSong%26author%3DN.%2BGuo%26author%3DC.%2BMa%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26author%3DW.%2BLi%26author%3DB.%2BLi%26title%3DModulating%2Bthe%2Bgraphitic%2Bdomains%2Band%2Bpore%2Bstructure%2Bof%2Bcorncob-derived%2Bhard%2Bcarbons%2Bby%2Bpyrolysis%2Bto%2Bimprove%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%26doi%3D10.3390%252Fmolecules28083595&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.3390%2Fmolecules28083595&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>176</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">533</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">541</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2015.07.059</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D176%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D533-541%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DW.%2BLv%26author%3DF.%2BWen%26author%3DJ.%2BXiang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhao%26author%3DL.%2BLi%26author%3DL.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BTian%26title%3DPeanut%2Bshell%2Bderived%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%2Bas%2Bultralong%2Bcycling%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Blithium%2Band%2Bsodium%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2015.07.059&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2015.07.059&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Peanut shell derived hard carbon as ultralong cycling anodes for lithium and sodium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lv, Weiming; Wen, Fusheng; Xiang, Jianyong; Zhao, Jing; Li, Lei; Wang, Limin; Liu, Zhongyuan; Tian, Yongjun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">176</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">533-541</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The peanut shells derived porous hard carbons (PSDHCs) by pyrolysis have been studied as anodes of Li/Na batteries (LIBs/NIBs).  Directly from the starting peanut shells, 600° is the favorable pyrolysis temp. for prepn. of the PSDHC sample (PSDHC-600) with the best electrochem. performances for LIB applications.  Also, from the activated peanut shells in KOH soln., the produced PSDHC-600A by pyrolysis at 600° is obsd. to offer greatly enhanced Li+/Na+ ion storage.  For LIB applications, PSDHC-600A delivers a retained capacity of 474 mA h g-1 after 400 cycles at 1 A g-1, larger than 314 mA h g-1 of PSDHC-600.  At a high current rate of 5 A g-1, PSDHC-600A sustains over 10000 cycles with no obvious sign of fade in capacity, and a capacity of 310 mA h g-1 is still retained.  For NIB applications, a capacity of 193 mA h g-1 is retained after 400 cycles at 0.25 A g-1, &gt;130 mA h g-1 of PSDHC-600.  Even at 1 A g-1, PSDHC-600A can be stably cycled over 3000 cycles, and a capacity of 129 mA h g-1 is still retained.  In comparison to PSDHC-600, the enhanced electrochem. properties of PSDHC-600A can be attributed to the finer porous structure with the increased percentage of nanoscale pores of diam. &lt;2 nm and the larger sp. surface area.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref24" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.diamond.2022.109329"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Piao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zou, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Navel orange peel-derived hard carbons as high performance anode materials of Na and Li-ion batteries</span>. <i>Diamond Relat.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biomass derived hard carbon used as a high performance anode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Kun-lei; Long, Qie; Zeng, Rui; Yi, Zi-qi; Zhang, Wei; Wang, Duo; Yin, Wei; Wu, Chao; Fan, Qing-jie; Zhang, Wu-xing; Huang, Yun-hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">32</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12733-12738</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A porous hard carbon material was synthesized by the simple pyrolysis of H3PO4-treated biomass, i.e., pomelo peels, at 700 °C in N2.  The as-obtained hard carbon had a 3D connected porous structure and a large sp. surface area of 1272 m2 g-1.  XPS anal. showed that the carbon material was functionalized by O-contg. and P-contg. groups.  The porous hard carbon was used as an anode for sodium ion batteries and exhibited good cycling stability and rate capability, delivering a capacity of 181 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 220 cycles and retaining a capacity of 71 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1.  The sodium storage mechanisms of the porous hard carbon can be explained by Na+ intercalation into the disordered graphene layers, redox reaction of the surface O-contg. functional groups and Na+ storage in the nanoscale pores.  However, the porous hard carbon demonstrated a low coulombic efficiency of 27%, resulting from the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase film and the side reactions of surface phosphorus groups.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref26" class="refNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit26" data-doi="10.1088/1674-1056/28/6/068203"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hard carbons derived from pine nut shells as anode materials for Na-ion batteries</span>. <i>Chinese Physics B</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>28</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">6</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">068203</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                10.1039/C4TA05451B</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D71%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DS.%2BXu%26author%3DX.%2BWu%26author%3DJ.%2BYu%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DY.-S.%2BHu%26author%3DH.%2BLi%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26author%3DX.%2BHuang%26title%3DAmorphous%2Bmonodispersed%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%2Bmicro-spherules%2Bderived%2Bfrom%2Bbiomass%2Bas%2Ba%2Bhigh%2Bperformance%2Bnegative%2Belectrode%2Bmaterial%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC4TA05451B&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC4TA05451B&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous monodispersed hard carbon micro-spherules derived from biomass as a high performance negative electrode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yunming; Xu, Shuyin; Wu, Xiaoyan; Yu, Juezhi; Wang, Yuesheng; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Huang, Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">71-77</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are expected to be a promising com. alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale and low-cost elec. energy storage applications in the near future.  Despite this, the absence of a suitable neg. electrode material hinders their development.  In this contribution, the authors synthesized monodispersed hard carbon spherules (HCS) from an abundant biomass of sucrose, and studied the influence of the carbonization temp. on the microstructure and electrochem. performance.  The initial coulombic efficiency of the HCS was increased to 83% by coating its surface with soft carbon through the pyrolysis of toluene.  The plateau capacity at the low potential region increased with increasing carbonization temp.  The HCS carbonized at 1600° showed the highest plateau capacity (220 mA-h/g) and excellent cycling performance with a capacity retention of 93% after 100 cycles.  When coupled with an air-stable P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 pos. electrode, the full cell exhibited a high initial coulombic efficiency of 76%, a mean operating voltage of 3.5 V and excellent cycling performance.  The theor. energy d. of this system is 200 W-h/kg.  These promising properties are believed to be close to the level required for practical applications.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref28" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/j.jechem.2020.07.025"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Insight to defects regulation on sugarcane waste-derived hard carbon anode for sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Journal of Energy Chemistry.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>55</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">499</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">508</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jechem.2020.07.025</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D55%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D499-508%26journal%3DJournal%2Bof%2BEnergy%2BChemistry.%26author%3DK.%2BYu%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BBai%26author%3DC.%2BWu%26title%3DInsight%2Bto%2Bdefects%2Bregulation%2Bon%2Bsugarcane%2Bwaste-derived%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%2Banode%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jechem.2020.07.025&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jechem.2020.07.025&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insight to defects regulation on sugarcane waste-derived hard carbon anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Kaihua; Wang, Xinran; Yang, Haoyi; Bai, Ying; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Energy Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">55</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">499-508</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JECOFG</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2095-4956</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Science Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A great deal of attention has been paid on developing plant-derived hard carbon (HC) materials as anodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  So far, the regulation of HC has been handicapped by the well-known ambiguity of Na+ storage mechanism, which fails to differentiate the Na+ adsorption and Na+ insertion, and their relationship with the size of d-interlayer spacing and structural porosity.  Herein, bagasse-derived HC materials have been synthesized through a combination of pyrolysis treatment and microwave activation.  The combined protocol has enabled to synergistically control the d-interlayer spacing and porosity.  Specifically, the microwave activation has created slit pores into HC and these pores allow for an enhanced Na+ adsorption with an increased sloping capacity, establishing a strong correlation between the porosity and sloping capacity.  Meanwhile, the pyrolysis treatment promotes the graphitization and it contributes to an intensified Na+ insertion with an increased plateau capacity, proving that the plateau capacity is largely contributed by the Na+ insertion between interlayers.  Therefore, the structural regulation of bagasse-derived HC has provided a proof on pos. explaining the Na+ storage with HC materials.  The structural changes in the pore size distribution, sp. surface area, d-interlayer spacing, and the electrochem. properties have been comprehensively characterized, all supporting our understanding of Na+ storage mechanism.  As a result, the HC sample with an optimized d-interlayer spacing and porosity has delivered an improved reversible capacity of 323.6 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1.  This work provides an understanding of Na+ storage mechanism and insights on enhancing the sloping/plateau capacity by rationally regulating the graphitization and porosity of HC materials for advanced SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1126/sciadv.abm7489"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Atomic Sn-enabled high-utilization, large-capacity and long-life Na anode</span>. <i>Sci.                 10.1016/j.carbon.2017.11.054</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D127%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D658-666%26journal%3DCarbon.%26author%3DQ.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BZhu%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DY.%2BFang%26author%3DX.%2BZhou%26author%3DJ.%2BBao%26title%3DRice%2Bhusk-derived%2Bhard%2Bcarbons%2Bas%2Bhigh-performance%2Banode%2Bmaterials%2Bfor%2Bsodium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.carbon.2017.11.054&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.carbon.2017.11.054&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Rice husk-derived hard carbons as high-performance anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Qiaoqiao; Zhu, Xiaoshu; Liu, Yuhan; Fang, Yuyan; Zhou, Xiaosi; Bao, Jianchun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">127</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">658-666</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have drawn ever-increasing attention for scalable elec. energy storage owing to the inexhaustible sources and wide distribution of sodium.  However, to develop feasible anode materials still remains a great challenge for the practical application of SIBs.  Here, the authors report hard carbons derived from a plentiful and deserted biomass of rice husk through a facile acid treatment and subsequent pyrolysis.  The study illustrates that the electrochem. properties of the rice husk-derived hard carbons (RHHCs) are significantly influenced by the pyrolysis temp. because of the discrepancy in their microstructure.  The RHHC pyrolyzed at 1300° (RHHC-1300) shows the highest reversible capacity of 372 mAh/g and good cycling stability and rate performance due to its large interlayer distance and suitable oxygen content.  Also, full sodium-ion batteries are assembled to examine the application prospect using Na3V2(PO4)2F3/C and RHHC-1300 as cathode and anode materials, resp., delivering a high-energy d. of 185 Wh/kg and stable cycling performance.  This work could intensify the fundamental understanding of the sodium storage mechanism in biomass-derived hard carbons.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref33" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/smll.202105568"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Long, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ning, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Modulating the Graphitic Domains of Hard Carbons Derived from Mixed Pitch and Resin to Achieve High Rate and Stable Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>18</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2105568</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.202105568</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D18%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2105568%26journal%3DSmall%26author%3DX.%2BYin%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BFeng%26author%3DZ.%2BLu%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DH.%2BLong%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BNing%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26title%3DModulating%2Bthe%2BGraphitic%2BDomains%2Bof%2BHard%2BCarbons%2BDerived%2Bfrom%2BMixed%2BPitch%2Band%2BResin%2Bto%2BAchieve%2BHigh%2BRate%2Band%2BStable%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fsmll.202105568&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fsmll.202105568&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Modulating the Graphitic Domains of Hard Carbons Derived from Mixed Pitch and Resin to Achieve High Rate and Stable Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yin, Xiuping; Zhao, Yufeng; Wang, Xuan; Feng, Xiaochen; Lu, Zhixiu; Li, Yong; Long, Hongli; Wang, Jing; Ning, Jinyan; Zhang, Jiujun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2105568</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Resin derived hard carbons (HCs) generally demonstrate remarkable electrochem. performance for both sodium ion batteries (SIBs) and potassium-ion batteries (KIBs), but their practical applications are hindered by their high price and high temp. pyrolysis (≈1500°C).  Herein, low-cost pitch is coated on the resin surface to compromise the cost, and meanwhile manipulate the microstructure at a relatively low pyrolysis temp. (1000°C).  HC-0.2P-1000 has a large no. of short graphitic layer structures and a relatively large interlayer spacing of 0.3743 nm, as well as ≈1 nm sized nanopores suitable for sodium storage.  Consequently, the as produced material demonstrates a superior reversible capacity (349.9 mAh g-1 for SIBs and 321.9 mAh g-1 for KIBs) and excellent rate performance (145.1 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1 for SIBs, 48.5 mAh g-1 at 20 A g-1 for KIBs).  Furthermore, when coupled with Na3V2(PO4)3 as cathode, the full cell exhibits a high energy d. of 251.1 Wh kg-1 and excellent stability with a capacity retention of 73.3% after 450 cycles at 1 A g-1.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.3c04984"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Duan, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Engineering ultrathin carbon layer on porous hard carbon boosts sodium storage with high initial coulombic efficiency</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>17</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">19063</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">19075</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span>. <i>Chem. Soc.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-ion batteries: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Myung, Seung-Taek; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Society Reviews</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3529-3614</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CSRVBR</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0306-0012</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy prodn. and storage technologies have attracted a great deal of attention for day-to-day applications.  In recent decades, advances in lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. have improved living conditions around the globe.  LIBs are used in most mobile electronic devices as well as in zero-emission electronic vehicles.  However, there are increasing concerns regarding load leveling of renewable energy sources and the smart grid as well as the sustainability of lithium sources due to their limited availability and consequent expected price increase.  Therefore, whether LIBs alone can satisfy the rising demand for small- and/or mid-to-large-format energy storage applications remains unclear.  To mitigate these issues, recent research has focused on alternative energy storage systems.  Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as the best candidate power sources because sodium is widely available and exhibits similar chem. to that of LIBs; therefore, SIBs are promising next-generation alternatives.  Recently, sodiated layer transition metal oxides, phosphates and org. compds. have been introduced as cathode materials for SIBs.  Simultaneously, recent developments have been facilitated by the use of select carbonaceous materials, transition metal oxides (or sulfides), and intermetallic and org. compds. as anodes for SIBs.  Apart from electrode materials, suitable electrolytes, additives, and binders are equally important for the development of practical SIBs.  Despite developments in electrode materials and other components, there remain several challenges, including cell design and electrode balancing, in the application of sodium ion cells.  In this article, we summarize and discuss current research on materials and propose future directions for SIBs.  This will provide important insights into scientific and practical issues in the development of SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref36" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">MenJun, L.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Classification Studies of Jujubes and Sour Jujubes</span>. <i>Jounal of HeBei Agricultural University</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1994</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">4</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">17</span></span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D1994%26pages%3D17%26journal%3DJounal%2Bof%2BHeBei%2BAgricultural%2BUniversity%26issue%3D4%26author%3DL.%2BMenJun%26title%3DClassification%2BStudies%2Bof%2BJujubes%2Band%2BSour%2BJujubes&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Li-ion battery materials: present and future</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nitta, Naoki; Wu, Feixiang; Lee, Jung Tae; Yushin, Gleb</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Materials Today (Oxford, United Kingdom)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">5</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">252-264</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">This review covers key technol. developments and scientific challenges for a broad range of Li-ion battery electrodes.  Periodic table and potential/capacity plots are used to compare many families of suitable materials.  Performance characteristics, current limitations, and recent breakthroughs in the development of com. intercalation materials such as lithium cobalt oxide (LCO), lithium nickel cobalt manganese oxide (NCM), lithium nickel cobalt aluminum oxide (NCA), lithium iron phosphate (LFP), lithium titanium oxide (LTO) and others are contrasted with that of conversion materials, such as alloying anodes (Si, Ge, Sn, etc.), chalcogenides (S, Se, Te), and metal halides (F, Cl, Br, I).  New polyanion cathode materials are also discussed.  The cost, abundance, safety, Li and electron transport, volumetric expansion, material dissoln., and surface reactions for each type of electrode materials are described.  Both general and specific strategies to overcome the current challenges are covered and categorized.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref41" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1039/D3GC02776G"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuan, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Densification pretreatment with a limited deep eutectic solvent triggers high-efficiency fractionation and valorization of lignocellulose</span>. <i>Green Chem.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">8026</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">8039</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-power lithium batteries from functionalized carbon-nanotube electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Seung Woo; Yabuuchi, Naoaki; Gallant, Betar M.; Chen, Shuo; Kim, Byeong-Su; Hammond, Paula T.; Yang, Shao-Horn</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Nanotechnology</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">531-537</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NNAABX</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1748-3387</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Much research has focused on increasing the power output of Li batteries by reducing Li-ion diffusion distances, but outputs remain far below those of electrochem. capacitors and below the levels required for many applications.  Here, the authors report an alternative approach based on the redox reactions of functional groups on the surfaces of C nanotubes.  Layer-by-layer techniques are used to assemble an electrode that consists of additive-free, densely packed and functionalized multiwalled C nanotubes.  The electrode, which is several micrometers thick, can store Li up to a reversible gravimetric capacity of ∼200 mA·h/g while also delivering 100 kW/kg of power and providing lifetimes in excess of thousands of cycles, both of which are comparable to electrochem. capacitor electrodes.  A device using the nanotube electrode as the pos. electrode and Li Ti oxide as a neg. electrode had a gravimetric energy ∼5 times higher than conventional electrochem. capacitors and power delivery ∼10 times higher than conventional Li-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref46" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1002/anie.202214717"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, F.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Dual function presodiation with sodium diphenyl ketone towards ultra stable hard carbon anodes for sodium ion batteries</span>. <i>Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2023</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>62</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">e202214717</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/anie.202214717</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D62%26publication_year%3D2023%26pages%3De202214717%26journal%3DAngew.%2BChem.%252C%2BInt.%2BEd.%26author%3DH.%2BFang%26author%3DS.%2BGao%26author%3DM.%2BRen%26author%3DY.%2BHuang%26author%3DF.%2BCheng%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26author%3DF.%2BLi%26title%3DDual%2Bfunction%2Bpresodiation%2Bwith%2Bsodium%2Bdiphenyl%2Bketone%2Btowards%2Bultra%2Bstable%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%2Banodes%2Bfor%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fanie.202214717&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fanie.202214717&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref47"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref47" class="refNumLink">47</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit47" data-doi="10.1021/acsenergylett.0c01712"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Le, P.                 10.1021/acsenergylett.0c01712</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D3212-3220%26journal%3DACS%2BEnergy%2BLett.%26author%3DY.%2BJin%26author%3DY.%2BXu%26author%3DP.%2BM.%2BLe%26author%3DT.%2BD.%2BVo%26author%3DQ.%2BZhou%26author%3DX.%2BQi%26author%3DJ.%2BG.%2BZhang%26title%3DHighly%2Breversible%2Bsodium%2Bion%2Bbatteries%2Benabled%2Bby%2Bstable%2Belectrolyte-electrode%2Binterphases%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsenergylett.0c01712&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsenergylett.0c01712&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Highly Reversible Sodium Ion Batteries Enabled by Stable Electrolyte-Electrode Interphases</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Yan; Xu, Yaobin; Le, Phung M. L.; Vo, Thanh D.; Zhou, Quan; Qi, Xingguo; Engelhard, Mark H.; Matthews, Bethany E.; Jia, Hao; Nie, Zimin; Niu, Chaojiang; Wang, Chongmin; Hu, Yongsheng; Pan, Huilin; Zhang, Ji-Guang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3212-3220</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AELCCP</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2380-8195</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium ion battery (NIB) is a promising alternative technol. for energy storage systems because of the abundance and low cost of sodium in the Earth's crust.  However, the limited cycle life and safety concerns of NIBs hinder their large-scale applications.  Here, we report a nonflammable localized high concn. electrolyte (sodium bis(fluorosulfonyl)imide-triethyl phosphate/1,1,2,2-tetrafluoroethyl-2,2,3,3-tetrafluoropropyl ether (1:1.5:2 in molar ratio)) for highly reversible NIBs.  By using a cryo-transmission electron microscope, it was found that an ultrathin (3 nm) and robust interphase layer formed on the cathode surface can block transition metal dissolns. and minimize surface reconstructions of the cathode.  The inorg.-rich solid electrolyte interphase formed on the hard carbon (HC) surface minimized undesirable reactions between HC and the electrolyte.  These stable interphases enabled high Coulombic efficiency and long-term stable cycling of the HC anode and the NaCu1/9Ni2/9Fe1/3Mn1/3O2 cathode.  The insights obtained in this work can be used to further improve the cycling stability and safety of rechargeable batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref48" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202310226"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Que, L.</span></span><span class="NLM_etal"></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Tea-Derived Sustainable Materials</span>. <i>Adv.                 10.1016/j.carbon.2020.11.004</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D173%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D253-261%26journal%3DCarbon%26author%3DD.%2BChen%26author%3DK.%2BLuo%26author%3DZ.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BZhong%26author%3DZ.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BSong%26author%3DX.%2BGuo%26title%3DDirect%2Bconversion%2Bof%2Bester%2Bbond-rich%2Bwaste%2Bplastics%2Binto%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%2Bfor%2Bhigh-performance%2Bsodium%2Bstorage%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.carbon.2020.11.004&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.carbon.2020.11.004&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Direct conversion of ester bond-rich waste plastics into hard carbon for high-performance sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Dequan; Luo, Kangying; Yang, Zhiwei; Zhong, Yanjun; Wu, Zhenguo; Song, Yang; Chen, Guang; Wang, Gongke; Zhong, Benhe; Guo, Xiaodong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">173</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">253-261</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0008-6223</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Disordered hard carbon (HC) has shown potential as the most promising anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  Pyrolyzing waste plastics is a sustainable alternative to obtain HC.  However, most plastics will completely decomp. without carbon residue or transform into highly graphitic carbon during the carbonation process because of lacking oxygen functional groups.  Hence, ester bond-rich waste engineering plastics, polycarbonate (PC), and polyethylene terephthalate (PET) were selected and directly converted into HC by a simple pyrolysis method.  The PC and PET-derived carbon anodes (PC-HC and PET-HC) exhibit high reversible capacities of 327 and 342 mAh·g-1 at 20 mA·g-1with remarkable initial coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 84.7% and 86.1%, resp.  Particularly, the carbon samples have no severe capacities decay after 140 cycles at 100 mA g-1.  This work provides a cost-effective, easily large-scale, and eco-friendly route to fabricate HC anodes for grid-scale energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref51" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201706294"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">N Do and defective nanographitic domain coupled hard carbon nanoshells for high performance lithium/sodium storage</span>. <i>Adv. Funct Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>28</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1706294</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201706294</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D28%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D1706294%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct%2BMater.%26author%3DS.%2BHuang%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DB.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DZ.%2BPeng%26author%3DR.%2BQi%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26title%3DN%2BDo%2Band%2Bdefective%2Bnanographitic%2Bdomain%2Bcoupled%2Bhard%2Bcarbon%2Bnanoshells%2Bfor%2Bhigh%2Bperformance%2Blithium%252Fsodium%2Bstorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.201706294&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.201706294&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref52" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.202200208"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yadegari, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tebyetekerwa, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ryan, M. P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Titirici, M.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Role of Hydrothermal Carbonization in Sustainable Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes</span>. <i>Adv. Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>12</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2200208</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/aenm.202200208</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D2200208%26journal%3DAdv.%2BEnergy%2BMater.%26author%3DZ.%2BXu%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BGuo%26author%3DF.%2BXie%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DH.%2BYadegari%26author%3DM.%2BTebyetekerwa%26author%3DM.%2BP.%2BRyan%26author%3DY.-S.%2BHu%26author%3DM.-M.%2BTitirici%26title%3DThe%2BRole%2Bof%2BHydrothermal%2BCarbonization%2Bin%2BSustainable%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%26doi%3D10.1002%252Faenm.202200208&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facs.langmuir.4c03504&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Faenm.202200208&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The Role of Hydrothermal Carbonization in Sustainable Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu, Zhen; Wang, Jing; Guo, Zhenyu; Xie, Fei; Liu, Haoyu; Yadegari, Hossein; Tebyetekerwa, Mike; Ryan, Mary P.; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Titirici, Maria-Magdalena</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2200208</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADEMBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1614-6840</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-Blackwell</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries as a prospective alternative to lithium-ion batteries are facing the challenge of developing high-performance, low-cost and sustainable anode materials.  Hard carbons are appropriate to store sodium ions, but major energy and environmental concerns during their fabrication process (i.e., high-temp. carbonization) have not been properly assessed.  Furthermore, the rational design of high-performing hard carbon anodes is usually limited by the conventional direct carbonization of org. precursors.  Here, the hydrothermal carbonization process is employed as a versatile pre-treatment method of renewable precursors, followed by high-temp. carbonization, for producing advanced hard carbon anodes.  The crit. role of hydrothermal pre-treatment in regulating the structure for an optimized performance of hard carbon anodes is elucidated, while revealing the sodium-ion storage mechanism using electrochem. kinetic calcns., advanced characterization and multi-scale modeling.  Furthermore, the environmental impacts of hydrothermal pre-treatment and subsequent carbonization are evaluated using life cycle assessment compared to direct carbonization.  By comparing hard carbon anodes with and without the hydrothermal pre-treatment, it is verified that the addnl. hydrothermal process is responsible for enhanced electrochem. performance, increased carbon yields and reduced carbon emissions.  The work provides a systematic understanding of functions and energy consumptions of hydrothermal systems to achieve next-generation sustainable sodium-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript"
